He is about 7,000 points behind No. 2 Karl Malone (36,928) and about 2,000 assists shy of No. 6 Oscar Robertson (9,887), with sizable gaps before Kobe Bryant and Isiah Thomas respectively at the No. 3 and No. 7 spots. So that\u2019s where I seem him landing before moving on to chase down NBA Franchise Owners in their various statistical categories. Shaun Powell :  It\u2019s a tricky question because nobody\u2019s sure how much longer LeBron intends to play (three more years at a high level is my guess because Father Time is undefeated). And we\u2019re not sure where he\u2019ll play after this season, which will also affect his role going forward. And yet: My guess is he\u2019ll finish higher on the scoring charts, naturally, maybe ahead of Kobe Bryant at No. 3 and in assists, either just above or just below Oscar Robertson, who sits at the No. 6 spot. That will juice the argument that LeBron is the best talent we\u2019ve ever seen, while Michael Jordan is the best all-around (player, winner). John Schuhmann : Given how well he\u2019s playing at the age of 33, it\u2019s hard to guess how many more years he\u2019ll play or if he\u2019ll ever miss more than just a few games to injury. But my best guess is No. 2 in scoring (in the 37,000 range) and No. 3 in assists (between 10 and 11,000). He has swapped out some of his mid-range shots for threes and is shooting those better, so he doesn\u2019t have to attack quite as much to stay in the 25-28 points-per-game range. Also, the Heat figured out how to best complement him (with shooting), the Cavs followed suit, and whatever team(s) he plays for going forward will know the same. So even if his scoring slows down, the assists will be there.  Sekou Smith : If he cared about such things, it would be fun to watch LeBron try to catch Kareem Abdul-Jabbar for No. 1 on the scoring list. He\u2019d have to play at this level until LeBron Jr. made it to the league and he\u2019d also have to continue to hone that 3-point stroke. But realistically, he could catch and pass Kobe Bryant for No. 3 and scare Karl Malone at No. 2 , provided he avoids significant injury and finishes his career as the centerpiece of whatever team(s) he plays for. The top five of the all-time assists list is going to be tough , even for a passer\/facilitator as gifted as LeBron has always been. But just being the same stratosphere as Magic Johnson (No. 5), Oscar Robertson (No. 6), Isiah Thomas (No. 7) and Gary Payton (No. 8) puts LeBron in unbelievable company. His ability to master so many different facets of the game is what will set him apart from so many of the other all-time greats. The also have the West\u2019s toughest schedule in regard to opponent strength, with their 14 January opponents having a cumulative winning percentage of 0.562 heading into the month. The Sixers have a slightly tougher slate in regard to cumulative opponent winning percentage, but 12 of Cleveland\u2019s 14 January games are against teams that are currently at or above .500. And the Cavs will play three games, including their visit to Boston on Wednesday, with a rest disadvantage (where they\u2019re playing the second game of a back-to-back and their opponent is not). The stretch between Christmas and the All-Star break can be a slog for some teams. Injuries and effort. Sorry, but anytime someone in or outside the game predicts great things for a young, tantalizing player, those two things \u2013 injuries and effort, among a dozen or a hundred potential hurdles \u2013 always should be baked into any projections. That didn\u2019t deter one NBA authority, however, from his prediction that New York Knicks big man Kristaps Porzingis one day will surpass Dallas\u2019 Dirk Nowitzki as arguably the best international player in league history. And as Marc Berman of the New York Post writes, this is from someone who knows a thing or two about the Mavericks\u2019 legend : All Porzingis needs to do over the next 15 years or so to breathe down Nowitzki\u2019s neck is close a gap of some 31,000 regular-season and postseason points, appear in 145 playoff games, make it to 13 All-Star Games, win an MVP award (with nine top-10 finishes) and win an NBA championship."},{"id":42512,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/oklahoma-city-thunder-trying-get-defense-back-track","date":"2018-01-01","title":"Oklahoma City Thunder trying to get defense back on track","content":"Offense comes, defense goes for Thunder Getting Paul George back from a one-game absence due to knee soreness? That\u2019s good. Sitting down Andre Roberson against Dallas Sunday with knee tendinitis? That\u2019s bad, and maybe of greater impact than George\u2019s return for an Oklahoma City team that has been sputtering defensively. Roberson\u2019s value to the Thunder is on the defensive end, both in his individual defense and his overall work in whatever scheme OKC coach Billy Donovan favors. But given his team\u2019s newfound issues \u2014 owing at least in part to limited practice time, per The Oklahoman \u2019s Eric Horne \u2014 Roberson was missed. Like so many assignments: In a 116-113 loss to Dallas to close out 2017, Donovan zeroed in on the Thunder defense\u2019s slippage, an inconvenience just as the offense has found its rhythm. Russell Westbrook had 38 points, 15 rebounds and 11 assists. George scored 25 points and Carmelo Anthony added 21. But the game was decided by Smith\u2019s slicing and dicing of the OKC defense, and Dallas\u2019 O shooting over the Thunder\u2019s D. Which is to say, in the NBA, there\u2019s always something that needs work."},{"id":42545,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-movie-storylines-were-norm-2017-carmelo-anthony-kyrie-irving","date":"2018-01-01","title":"Fire up the popcorn! Movie-like storylines were norm in NBA last year","content":" Finally got to see \u201cThe Last Jedi\u201d on Saturday. Regular movie attendance is a hazard of aging (you stay home more when you\u2019re married), of being a parent, of a job that often requires working weekends. I haven\u2019t seen any of the last six or seven movies that won Best Picture at the Oscars. So, seeing Luke Skywalker and the gang on the last weekend of 2017 was a rare treat, and a reminder of how quickly the past 12 months went by. Time is so ephemeral, and moments that seem so large at the time can quickly be swamped and forgotten with the advent of the next big thing. That\u2019s why it\u2019s important to stop and reflect on what\u2019s just happened, so we don\u2019t forget the lessons learned in the moment and don\u2019t repeat the mistakes we\u2019ve made. The NBA\u2019s big moments of 2017 stretched from coast to coast, inspiring and challenging both those who participated in them and those who witnessed them. They impacted the league\u2019s elite teams and its also-rans, and like the silver screen, created heroes and villains, winners and losers, as we got our figurative popcorn ready to watch the show. Here then are the top 10 NBA stories of 2017, introduced by some of my all-time favorite films: David Griffin, the very successful general manager of the Cleveland Cavaliers, enters 2017 in the final year of his contract \u2014 and, understandably, would like to be paid commensurate with what the top GMs in the league get paid. The Cavaliers resist, and who knows why \u2014 the already huge outlay for salaries? The sense that anyone could successfully manage a team built around LeBron James? Nor do they give Griffin permission to interview with the Orlando Magic or Atlanta Hawks , each of whom seek it. By the end of June, after The Finals , Griffin is hard at work trying to put together potential deals to bring either Jimmy Butler or Paul George to Cleveland to play with James next season, and there is at least some traction on a three-team deal that would have sent Butler to the Cavs and Kevin Love to the Denver Nuggets. But all potential Griffin-driven deals are silenced June 19, when Griffin and the team announce that after a final discussion with owner Dan Gilbert about his future, they\u2019ll part ways at the end of the month . The decision throws one of the league\u2019s top two franchises into chaos, leaving it without the guy who brought Love from Minnesota , J.R. Smith and Iman Shumpert from New York and Kyle Korver from Atlanta . Griffin also elevated Tyronn Lue from assistant coach to coach in 2016 , replacing David Blatt \u2014 who\u2019d led the Cavs to The Finals in 2015 . The move was roasted at the time; Lue and James and Griffin had the last word six months later, with the first championship parade for a major sports team in Cleveland since 1964 . The Cavs stayed in-house for their replacement, elevating assistant GM Koby Altman to the full-time GM gig. You thought Darth Vader and Luke had a complicated relationship? Jeanie Buss, the Lakers\u2019 controlling owner and president, goes hard in February to restructure the team\u2019s front office following years of questionable personnel decisions and coaching hires. She fires her brother, Jimmy, the former executive vice president and primary decision maker for on-court basketball decisions, as well as longtime General Manager Mitch Kupchak, replacing them, respectively, with Hall of Famer Magic Johnson and high-profile player agent Rob Pelinka . (The team also dismisses longtime PR head John Black.) The moves aligned with what the Buss family\u2019s patriarch and the team\u2019s longtime owner, the late Dr. Jerry Buss, clearly wanted after his death \u2014 for Jeanie to run the team after he was gone . The massive changes tie Jeanie and Magic, with whom she had grown close while he was the franchise\u2019s supernova player , as the team\u2019s chief decision makers going forward, as the Lakers try desperately to accelerate their rebuild in the post-Kobe Bryant era. Phil Jackson\u2019s unfulfilling stint as president of the Knicks comes to a sudden end after three years in June , just after Jackson takes French point guard Frank Ntilikina No. 8 overall in the 2017 Draft . Jackson\u2019s reign was not a total bust \u2014 he took Kristaps Porzingis fourth overall in the 2015 , to the consternation of the always-consternated fan base, but Jackson was proven right about the 7-foot Latvian\u2019s immense offensive potential. And New York did bring in decent role players during Jackson\u2019s term like Kyle O\u2019Quinn and Willy Hernangomez. Yet Jackson was never able to get his team to embrace the triangle offense he insisted could still work in the NBA, in part because he was no longer physically able to coach. He tried to instill it through a sort of osmosis, even though his coaches \u2014 including the last one he hired, Jeff Hornacek \u2014 clearly wanted to play a different style. Jackson was known to come down during practices to show players the finer points of the triangle \u2014 not the best look for the actual coach of the team at the time. And Jackson\u2019s once-strong relationship with Carmelo Anthony also frayed, as he began saying publicly that trading Anthony would be in the best interests of the franchise \u2014 which was true. But Jackson\u2019s odd tack of pointing out Anthony\u2019s shortcomings as an aging superstar did nothing to help his leverage in trade talks, or to get Anthony to waive the no-trade clause that Jackson had inexplicably given him when the Knicks re-signed Anthony to a five-year, $128 million deal in 2014 . Porzingis was so befuddled by how the team treated Anthony that he skipped his own exit interviews at the end of the regular season. The last straw for Jackson came when he said in an interview with the MSG Network, the team\u2019s house station, that he was willing to talk about trading Porzingis , who had displayed significant offensive potential in his first two seasons, to help the team\u2019s \u201cfuture.\u201d At that moment, Porzingis was 21 years old. The Knicks named longtime MSG executive Steve Mills as the team\u2019s new president; Mills hired veteran executive Scott Perry as his new GM. Gordon Hayward is beloved in Salt Lake City, the cornerstone of the Utah Jazz\u2019s painstaking rebuild after it traded Deron Williams to the Nets in 2011 and started over. Hayward, the team\u2019s first-round pick in 2010 , makes himself into a superstar during his seven seasons in Utah, which goes from 25 wins in 2013-14 to 38, 40 and 51 wins by 2016-17. That season, Hayward made his first All-Star team, averaging 21.9 points and 5.4 rebounds, shooting nearly 40 percent on 3-pointers. After the Jazz won a playoff series for the first time in seven years, Hayward entered unrestricted free agency in July, with several teams in hot pursuit \u2014 led by the Boston Celtics and Miami Heat, with Utah trying to re-sign him as well. After taking his visits, Hayward is primed to make his decision via the Players\u2019 Tribune, the preferred method these days for athletes to get their views out, unfiltered. But ESPN\u2019s Chris Haynes ruins the rollout by breaking the news : Hayward picked Boston, breaking the heart of Jazz nation and elating the Celtics, who had targeted him for months, if not longer. It made Hayward\u2019s gruesome season-ending injury just minutes into his Boston career even more devastating. That Les Alexander decided to sell the Houston Rockets after owning them for 24 years wasn\u2019t a surprise, even though Alexander had no health issues and certainly didn\u2019t need the money. Everyone, sooner or later, cashes in, and the 72-year-old Alexander was ready to walk away from the franchise that he helped lead to consecutive NBA titles  in the 1990s . What was surprising was the speed of the sale to local businessman, reality TV star and entrepreneur Tillman Fertitta. And what was shocking was the price tag: $2.2 billion, the biggest sale of an NBA team in history , topping the $2 billion Steve Ballmer paid for the LA Clippers in 2014 . While the sale price surely reflected the labor peace the NBA currently enjoys, the huge national TV deal in place through 2024, market size and quality of the franchise, it also reinforced the idea that the Ballmer deal wasn\u2019t an outlier, and NBA teams may well continue selling at or near those prices in the future. The NFL was crippled this season when players began emulating Colin Kaepernick and taking a knee during the playing of the national anthem to protest what they feel is police brutality around the country. That the protests were co-opted politically by opponents who conflated the player protests with being anti-military or somehow protesting the flag didn\u2019t matter; the damage was done.  NBA players didn\u2019t take such drastic steps, perhaps in part because the league has specific rules regarding standing for the anthem . But they didn\u2019t have to, because they\u2019d been so outspoken about so many deaths of African-Americans over the years that occurred under specious circumstances \u2014 Trayvon Martin, Eric Garner and the like. Chief among the most outspoken players has been LeBron James, and he continued that on Sept. 23, when he went after President Trump, who\u2019d \u201cdisinvited\u201d the Golden State Warriors from the White House for the traditional championship team photo op (the Warriors had said they weren\u2019t going, anyway) and criticized Stephen Curry for \u201chesitating\u201d to accept the invite. James\u2019 retort soon went viral \u2014 and brought back the word \u201cbum\u201d to the American lexicon, if only for a while \u2014 and remains one of the most popular Tweets in history, with more than 1.5 million recorded \u201clikes\u201d as of this morning. The President did not respond to James\u2019 tweet, a marked departure from his usual pattern of almost immediately firing back on social media against anyone who criticizes him by name. And the players\u2019 stances are reinforced by several NBA coaches, who also go in on Trump early and often: Gregg Popovich , Steve Kerr and Stan Van Gundy chief among them. That there was very little public and\/or financial blowback for any of those teams because their respective coaches spoke out, and no public rebukes by their team\u2019s owners, either, spoke to the vast difference in just about everything between the NFL and NBA. Isaiah Thomas has a great individual season in leading the Boston Celtics to the Eastern Conference finals \u2014 he makes his second All-Star team, finishes third in the league in scoring (28.9 per game) , seventh in PER, fifth in three-pointers made, second in Offensive Win Shares \u2014 and leads the NBA in fourth-quarter scoring . And none of that matters when his world is shattered by the death of his younger sister, Chyna, in an automobile accident in Washington state just before the start of the playoffs. Playing through his grief, he twice scores 33 points in Boston\u2019s six-game victory over Chicago in the first round, flies across the country after the clinching win on a Friday, attends his sister\u2019s funeral in Washington state Saturday morning, then flies back across the country Saturday afternoon, not arriving back in Boston until 3 a.m. Sunday \u2014 with a 12:30 p.m. tipoff Sunday afternoon against Washington in the first game of the conference semis . Thomas again goes for 33 in a Game 1 win \u2014 getting a tooth knocked out in the process \u2014 and then puts on a performance for the ages three days later in Game 2 . Hurtling himself into the Wizards\u2019 defense in the second half, Thomas leads the Celtics back from a 14-point third-quarter deficit and a six-point deficit in the last three minutes of regulation, hitting shots from all over, again and again, in the fourth quarter and in overtime. In the last 17 minutes of play, Thomas scores 29 of his 53 points, driving the Celtics to an improbable Game 2 win \u2014 on what would have been his sister\u2019s 23rd birthday. It gave one chills, and pause , at what an athlete at the highest level of focus can achieve. The Oklahoma City Thunder\u2019s Russell Westbrook and the Rockets\u2019 James Harden battle all season long, superlative for superlative, highlight for highlight, in a quest for league Most Valuable Player honors. Harden becomes the first player ever to score 2,000 points and assist on 2,000 points in a season , and becomes the first player ever to score 2,000, grab 600 rebounds and dish out 900 assists in one season. The 4,554 points he personally accounted for in \u201916-\u201917 were the most ever by one man in one year. And, yet, Westbrook was just as incredible . He leads the league in scoring at 31.6 points per game, while adding 10.7 rebounds and 10.4 assists \u2014 equaling one of the great sports records that many thought couldn\u2019t be matched: Oscar Robertson\u2019s 1961-62 season, the last in which an NBA player averaged a triple-double . He does so with a team that, charitably, lacks consistent perimeter shooting, and is without another star player, Kevin Durant having left the summer before via free agency for the Golden State Warriors . In the end, Westbtrook wins Kia MVP honors , having had to accomplish something no one had done in more than 50 years to hold off Harden and his excellence. Kevin Durant joined the Warriors with one mandate: win the NBA championship. Nothing else would justify Durant\u2019s decision to leave the Thunder for the team that had just vanquished OKC in the 2016 Western Conference finals , in seven excruciating games \u2014 and even a ring wouldn\u2019t satisfy those who hated KD the most. There were some ups and downs during the regular season, as Durant found his way and Stephen Curry and the incumbent Warriors figured out how to recalibrate themselves around Durant. But Golden State got some traction late in the regular season after Durant returned from a knee injury , plowed through the Western Conference with ease in the playoffs and faced LeBron James and the Cavaliers for a third straight year in The Finals. Back on the biggest stage for the first time since 2011, Durant rises to the moment: a five-game average of 37.2 points , 8.2 rebounds and 5.4 assists, shooting 55.6 percent from the floor \u2014 including 47.4 percent on threes. The Warriors take the title back, and Durant takes home Finals MVP honors , having slayed all the dragons, beaten back all the haters and reaching the peak \u2014 on and off the court. There have been offseasons with significant deals before. There have been trades involving superstars before. But rarely has there been one offseason with so much of both. It began three days before the Draft, three days before the Draft, when Philly and Boston swap positions \u2014 the 76ers gave the Celtics a first-round pick either in 2018 or 2019 in order to move up from No. 3 in the 2017 Draft to No. 1, with the intent of taking University of Washington guard Markelle Fultz. The next night, Atlanta gets out from the remaining two years of Dwight Howard\u2019s contract by sending him to Charlotte , willing to take on the extra years of Miles Plumlee\u2019s contract along with Marco Belinelli. Two days later, on Draft night, the Bulls send three-time All-Star Jimmy Butler and the No. 16 pick to Minnesota for Kris Dunn, Zach LaVine and the No. 7 pick overall \u2014 Lauri Markkanen of Arizona . Four days after that, the LA Clippers, with no real choice, start blowing up their roster. They send the heart of their status as a legit title contender \u2014 nine-time All-Star point guard Chris Paul \u2014 to the Rockets (who\u2019ve long coveted him) for guard Patrick Beverley, forward Sam Dekker, Lou Williams and a lot of other players and picks the Rockets had to acquire and otherwise cobble together to make the numbers work. The Rockets then quickly move to try and add Carmelo Anthony. On July 1 \u2014 the first night of free agency \u2013 the Indiana Pacers get into the act by dealing four-time All-Star Paul George to Oklahoma City for Victor Oladipo and Domantas Sabonis. Cleveland is soon rocked by Kyrie Irving\u2019s trade demands becoming public. A month later, the Cavs\u2019 new GM, Koby Altman, sends Irving to Boston, of all places , getting All-Star guard Isaiah Thomas back in a package that includes, most importantly, the unprotected 2018 first-rounder from Brooklyn that the Celtics have held onto and refused to included in other potential trades. And the Knicks\u2019 new braintrust finally ends the Anthony saga in New York just before the start of camp in late September, sending him not to Houston, but to Oklahoma City to join George and Russell Westbrook, for Enes Kanter, Doug McDermott and a 2018 second-rounder. The NBA landscape had been, in one summer, turned upside down. (Coda: \u201cThe Last Jedi\u201d is very good. The rebuild was set in motion by trading Jimmy Butler to the Timberwolves last June , with point guard Kris Dunn, wing Zach LaVine and first-round pick Lauri Markkanen getting big minutes and absorbing all the Ls that young teams get. Things were exacerbated when Bobby Portis punched teammate Nikola Mirotic in the face during a practice altercation two days before the start of the season; Mirotic suffered facial fractures and a concussion, and missed Chicago\u2019s first 23 games recovering. Portis was suspended for eight games without pay. When Mirotic returned Dec. 8 , the Bulls were 3-20, having lost games by 49 at Golden State, 39 at San Antonio and 30 at Utah. The plan, though painful, was well on its way to fruition. But then, strange things started happening. Mirotic returned and played the best basketball of his career coming off the bench (even though he and Portis, understandably, are still on the outs). Unheralded, undrafted David Nwaba, the former Los Angeles Lakers guard who was a waiver claim in July, came back after missing 12 games and started providing outstanding two-way play . The Bulls began playing with the pace that Fred Hoiberg has desperately sought since becoming the team\u2019s coach. And Chicago, improbably, started winning. The Bulls beat Charlotte Dec. 8 and New York the next night, then blew out Boston by 23 and avenged the loss to the Jazz. They won at Milwaukee and beat then-hot Philadelphia, then throttled the Magic Dec. 20. In 12 days, they\u2019d won seven games in row. They\u2019ve cooled off a little since then, but they\u2019re still playing very good basketball \u2014 and jeopardizing their chances at a high pick, at least until they move Mirotic (they can\u2019t trade him until Jan. 15) and veteran center Robin Lopez, who\u2019s been very good in the middle. And Dunn, the 23-year-old who\u2019d flamed out in one desultory season of horrific shooting for Tom Thibodeau in Minnesota before being dealt, found his footing, both as a scorer and a floor general. He\u2019d been too good in college \u2014 a second-team All-American his senior season at Providence, where he worked and trained with God Shammgod. The former NBA player and fellow Friar \u2014 legendary for the crossover dribble that bears his name \u2014 was back at his alma mater as a grad assistant. Dunn\u2019s offensive rating leaped from 97.1 in November to 100.9 in December ; his assists rose from 4.3 to 7.8. He made a huge 3-pointer down the stretch to tie the game with Philly, and two more buckets to salt the game away. He broke down the Bucks for six points late and made two free throws with seven seconds left Friday to help beat New York. \u201cThe biggest thing I\u2019ve seen out of Kris is just his overall consistency at both,\u201d Hoiberg said Sunday. \u201cHe showed flashes early of really being in a stance, and then he\u2019d take plays off. But now, he\u2019s out there with a great focus and mentality. And the most impressive thing about Kris is just how he\u2019s learned to help finish games. It\u2019s not easy at this level.\u201d Shooting 3-pointers is still a work in progress for Dunn, but he\u2019s better than he was last season. And the Bulls are better than anyone thought they\u2019d be \u2014 and, frankly, than most of their fans want them to be. Me: How much of your improvement in the last few weeks is getting more comfortable with the speed of the game, and how much is guys like Mirotic and Portis getting back on the floor who can help you finish? Kris Dunn: I think Fred (Hoiberg) also helped me. He liked to play with a fast pace, get in the lane, be aggressive at the rim. We\u2019ve got a lot of shooters spread out when we can spread out. His offense helps. And when you\u2019ve got shooters around you, it\u2019s easier to get in the lane, especially when they\u2019re making shots. Everything opens up. I think we all watch a lot of film, and we\u2019re all starting to get used to each other. The chemistry\u2019s building. I think everybody knows their role on the team, so I think that helped us. Me: Was there any game in particular where it started clicking for you? KD: I can\u2019t really remember a game. But each and every game, I feel like I\u2019m improving, getting more comfortable, getting better. There\u2019s going to be bad games. There\u2019s 82 games; you can\u2019t be perfect all the time. But I\u2019m starting to learn, in order to be an elite player, you\u2019ve got to build consistent games. That\u2019s what I\u2019m trying to work on. Me: When you get your individual cutups from Paul (Miller, the Bulls\u2019 video coordinator), what\u2019s the first thing you look at? KD: Right now, just my pace. Pace is everything with this team. When we have good pace, and we\u2019re running out in transition, swinging the ball, I think we\u2019ve a good team. So I look at pace. Then I look at my decision making \u2014 was that the right read, at the right time? Turnovers. And then I go look at the defense. Me: Why are you more successful now making plays at the ends of games? KD: The game\u2019s slowing down for me at a tremendous rate. Last year, I couldn\u2019t even tell you what position \u2014 one, two, three. I\u2019m just out there, trying to impress the coach. That was what it was, and I couldn\u2019t really learn. This year I\u2019m learning. I\u2019m playing the role I\u2019m used, point guard. I\u2019m huge on film, so I watch a lot of film, see what I do wrong, see what I\u2019m doing good. Honestly, it\u2019s really slowing down for me. Me: Do you learn more from when you execute successfully at the ends of games, or when you don\u2019t? KD: When you don\u2019t succeed. When you succeed, it feels good. But when you don\u2019t succeed, you go back and look at the film, see what you missed, or if somebody else was open. Why the shot didn\u2019t go in. Every day, you can\u2019t be a hero, and I understood that. Me: Any point guards around the league you look at to see how they handle end of game situations? KD: Naw. To be honest, I look at Kobe, his mentality. He enjoys that situation. He always wants the ball. I study him a lot when it comes down the stretch, his footwork, being able to get to his spot. Even if the defender knows what spot he\u2019s going to go to, but still be able to get to that spot and still raise up and be able to make the play, that\u2019s fascinated me. I watch a lot of him. Me: Has the game gotten so 3-point heavy that there\u2019s more opportunities in the mid-post and for mid-range players than people realize? KD: Yeah. Nowadays, fours, they\u2019ve got to be able to shoot the ball, stretch the floor out. A person like me who likes to be aggressive, stay downhill, that helps me out a lot. \u2018Cause now I can either spray it out, or I can get the four man on me \u2014 he\u2019s got to switch. You\u2019ve got the four man on you, (it\u2019s) pick your poison kind of thing. I think the game evolving is a good thing for a lot of bigs, but it\u2019s even better on the guards, \u2018cause you can get to the basket. Me: But you\u2019re getting more comfortable shooting the three? KD: Yeah, definitely am. I\u2019m\u2019a keep shooting it. I\u2019ve got a lot of years ahead of me; I want to get comfortable with it. The more you shoot it, the more you get comfortable there, the more you\u2019ll be able to tweak the kinds of things you\u2019re doing wrong. You can make it more polished. I\u2019m gonna try to do it now, while I\u2019m young, so as the years come by I can make those tweaks in the offseason, and make it more polished. Me: How much are you staying in touch with Shammgod? KD: Oh, man, we talk, at least twice a week. That\u2019s my guy. He\u2019s doing an unbelievable job with Dennis (Smith, the Mavericks\u2019 rookie point guard) and all the other players. One thing about Sham, he\u2019s a good mentor of giving people confidence. Even when you feel like you\u2019re in a dark place, he\u2019s good at giving people confidence. Me: I imagine that was very necessary last year for you? KD: Yeah. You know, I knew it was going to be tough, coming in. I sensed it. I ain\u2019t know to deal with it at first. This was the first time I ever had to come off the bench, first time I didn\u2019t know what the coach wanted from me, and etcetera. It was a point in time during the season when I told myself, I can\u2019t let this get to me. My family\u2019s seen my whole personality change and everything, so I had to change it in the summer. I had to put in more work than I did the year before. I got a great group around me \u2014 my family, my friends, Shammgod. And he reached out to me to make sure I was doing the right things. It was really up to me to bounce back. Me: You\u2019ve got a young group here that\u2019s got a chance to get better. But you know that some of these guys could get dealt by the deadline. Is it hard to grow with this group not knowing what the future\u2019s going to bring? KD: Yeah, it definitely is. These guys are a great group of guys. Their character is unbelievable. It\u2019s going to throw the chemistry off a little bit (if) guys get traded. As a team, we\u2019re going to have to find a way to get through that. If they don\u2019t get traded, it\u2019s a blessing for us. We\u2019re playing good basketball. Everybody\u2019s starting to understand what their role is, and the chemistry is off the charts. It\u2019s tough to say. At the same time, it\u2019s a business \u2014 control what you can control. \u2014 Washington Nationals star outfielder Bryce Harper ( @Bharper3407 ), Wednesday, 2:46 p.m., after the Wizards unveiled their version of their City uniforms \u2014 which are, to be sure, fire. \u201c My son actually told me before the game, \u2018Daddy, I want you to make five threes.\u2019 I told him I will try. I can\u2019t promise. But I made eight actually. So I\u2019m sure he\u2019s very happy. And he was at the game too.\u201d \u2014 Nikola Mirotic , after scoring 28 points in 27 minutes in the improbable Bulls\u2019 ninth win in their last 11 games on Friday, over New York. \u201c The fans, the media wrote him off before he even went out and played. That\u2019s what I was upset about. You don\u2019t give him a chance to go out there and do what he\u2019s supposed to do. Give him a chance and then go from there. Just don\u2019t shoot him down because you\u2019re looking at the money. Because that\u2019s all you\u2019re looking at. You\u2019re not looking at his game and how he got better. You\u2019re looking at his money and you don\u2019t have to because everyone is getting paid [well] in this business. And Tim worked his tail off to get paid.\u201d \u2014 Tim Hardaway, Sr. , now a Pistons assistant coach, to the New York Post , defending his son Tim, Jr., from criticism that Sr. (correctly) felt was and is centered on the four-year, $71 million offer sheet from the Knicks to Hardaway, Jr., that the Hawks declined to match last summer. \u201dIt\u2019s basketball, it\u2019s not the Middle East peace process. From William Proctor: No, they\u2019re not tanking anymore; this is an old-fashioned slump, brought about chiefly by regression on defense \u2014 which has been exacerbated by Embiid\u2019s absences (six of Philly\u2019s last 11 games through Saturday; not surprisingly, Philly is 0-6 in the games he\u2019s missed). Ben Simmons\u2019 defensive rating, for example, has blown up to 103.2 in December after being at 100.5 in November . He hasn\u2019t forgotten how to play defense; when you don\u2019t have that 7-foot equalizer in the back, your overplays and gambles tend to be exposed rather than rewarded. Robert Covington\u2019s shooting has slipped ( 28.1 percent since coming back Dec. 15 ). I don\u2019t think he\u2019s forgotten how to shoot, but it\u2019s a lot harder when defenses don\u2019t have to put two people in Embiid\u2019s lap and can jam the 3-point line. I think coach Brett Brown laid it out plainly last week: \u201cwe are third in the NBA defensively and sixth offensively with Joel. We go down to 29th defensively and 21st offensively without him. It\u2019s night and day. He is our crown jewel, that\u2019s the bottom line.\u201d Handling his solo. From Cole Bertlesen: Absolutely, Cole. People around the league know how impressive Mitchell has been and the circumstances under which he\u2019s achieving those numbers. Market size has no impact, as the fact that four of the last five Rookies of the Year played for the Minnesota Timberwolves, Milwaukee Bucks and Portland Trail Blazers should prove. Donovan will get a lot of first-place votes if he keeps this up and I\u2019d be very surprised if he\u2019s not, at worst, in the top three by the end of the season. Take off the shackles? From Kenn Becker Quiles: That won\u2019t happen, Kenn, because the league has made offensive flow and movement a priority over the last 20 years\u2019 worth of rules changes. The illegal defense adaptation in 1983 was designed specifically to discourage NBA teams from playing zone defenses regularly, since you normally plant a defender in the middle of the paint in most zone coverages and leave him there. The defensive 3-second violation means the paint will almost always be open for drivers, and that\u2019s what the league wants \u2014 talented ballhandlers, in space, playing downhill. There are, simply, more great guards than great big men, and the NBA has believed for some time now that fans want more offense. The advent of the 3-pointer as a primary weapon was the inevitable result of finding more and easier ways to put points on the board. The best way to ensure constant end-to-end action is to give the best players more opportunities to score. Clogging the paint with bigs would reduce those opportunities. (Last week\u2019s averages in parenthesis) 1) James Harden (30.8 ppg, 4 rpg, 9.8 apg, .392 FG, .875 FT): Just 37 assists shy of passing Allen Leavell (3,339) for second place on the franchise\u2019s all-time list, behind Calvin Murphy (4,402). 2) LeBron James (21.7 ppg, 8 rpg, 8.7 apg, .439 FG, .706 FT): Turned 33 on Saturday, at which time he was a) averaging the most points in his career in eight years; b) averaging the most assists per game in his career; c) shooting better than 40 percent on threes for just the second time in his career. 3) Giannis Antetokounmpo (24.3 ppg, 9.7 rpg, 4.3 apg, .604 FG, .800 FT): \u201cPlays like an angel every night\u201d could be one of the best calls for a player ever. 4) Kevin Durant (23.3 ppg, 5.4 rpg, 5.4 apg, .500 FG, .957 FT): Kia Defensive Player of the Year chatter building with KD\u2019s spike this season in blocked shots, but let\u2019s keep in mind that Draymond Green (100), Klay Thompson (100.8) and Stephen Curry (102.9) all have defensive ratings higher than Durant\u2019s (103.6) per NBA.com\/Stats. That\u2019s not at all meant to denigrate KD\u2019s improved defense, only to point out that Golden State defensive excellence stems from multiple players being able to switch and guard in space. 5) Kyrie Irving (26.3 ppg, 4.5 rpg, 4.8 apg, .461 FG, .938 FT): Career-best efficiency grounded in fewer minutes so far this season \u2014 32.4 compared with 35.1 last year. 16 \u2014 Consecutive wins by the San Antonio Spurs over the Brooklyn Nets in San Antonio, a streak that continued with last Tuesday\u2019s Spurs win over Brooklyn . The Nets\u2019 last franchise win in San Antonio was on Jan. 22, 2002 , when Jason Kidd and Kenyon Martin starred, and ultimately led the then-New Jersey Nets to the NBA Finals. 40 \u2014 Days between wins at Moda Center for the Trail Blazers, which isn\u2019t good, considering it\u2019s their home court. Portland broke a six-game home losing streak there last Thursday, coming back from 18 down in the third quarter to beat Philadelphia; the Blazers\u2019 last home win had come on Nov. 18 over Sacramento. .578 \u2014 Three-point percentage (37 of 64) in December for New Orleans Pelicans\u2019 guard E\u2019Twaun Moore , quietly off to an insanely efficient start for New Orleans \u2014 the only holdback is his 61 percent form from the foul line. Otherwise, he\u2019s off the charts offensivelly \u2014 54 percent overall from the floor, 47 percent on threes, .633 Effective Field Goal percentage, .635 True Shooting Percentage \u2014 in averaging a career-best 13.3 points per game. 1) Happy 2018, everybody. I think we can all agree that while between the lines in the NBA, a lot went right in 2017, outside of many of those arenas, chaos and uncertainty and anger reined. May we all be more comforted, more united, but also more willing to speak up and speak out in the coming 12 months when we see injustice and unfair treatment of those who can\u2019t fight back. 2 ) I have a sense that the trade deadline, thought by many to likely be dull because so many teams are capped out or close to it, is going to be a little livelier than we all think. With small ball now dominant throughout the league, there are lots of good players who could help teams a player short flourish in the playoffs. The Bulls will almost certainly deal Nikola Mirotic, who\u2019s flourished in Chicago since his return, with a contract that\u2019s very affordable ($29 million through 2019, if the Bulls pick up the second-year option on his deal before sending him out). Vince Carter is 40, but he just put 24 on the Cavs , and he\u2019s only making $8 million, which is now closer to $4 million for a contending team on a pro-rated basis. The Lakers won\u2019t re-sign Julius Randle, who\u2019s been great for them off the bench all season, and have to move him by the deadline. With Enes Kanter playing so well, the Knicks will likely move one of their surplus bigs, either one of which is very serviceable: Kyle O\u2019Quinn or Willy Hernangomez. It\u2019s hard to believe Atlanta won\u2019t move Marco Belinelli (39 percent on 3-pointers), and that disappointing Charlotte won\u2019t soon be in selling mode, with vets like Marvin Williams and\/or Jeremy Lamb having value. 3) Kudos to Phoenix Coach Jay Triano for knowing the rules and directing Tyson Chandler to redirect a last-second inbounds pass from Dragan Bender into the basket to beat Memphis. Almost no one, starting with me, knew that touching an inbounded pass that goes above the cylinder and putting it in the basket cannot be called offensive goaltending. That rule certainly will be changed before the start of next season, but Triano won a game for his team by being sharp and on top of his Xs and Os, and good for him. 4) With or (preferably) without profanity, The Science Guy speaks for me . At some point, you either accept that an apple is an apple and not a kumquat, you know what I\u2019m saying? I\u2019m done with too-clever people who think questioning everything shows how evolved they are compared with the rest of us dullards. We can\u2019t all just stick our heads (figuratively) in the sand and say \u2018well, how do you know humans didn\u2019t live with dinosaurs?\u2019 We build our base of knowledge on what others before us have taught and come to believe, based on their own learning, and we continue to refine and improve upon what we\u2019ve all come to accept as \u201cfact.\u201d If we don\u2019t agree on certain things, societies cease to exist. We all agree that we stop driving our cars when the light turns red. It\u2019s not something we debate; we don\u2019t accept the opinions of those who might say, \u2018well, stopping on red infringes on my freedoms.\u201d We. Don\u2019t. Do. It. We stop on red. And the damn earth is round. 1) It\u2019s not Tony Brothers\u2019 or Gediminas Petraitis\u2019 fault that they missed five (!) traveling calls in the last two minutes of Thursday\u2019s wild 99-98 Boston win over Houston , according to the league\u2019s own Last Two Minutes report. That\u2019s why the NBA went to three-referee crews beginning with the 1988-89 season \u2014 two-man crews just couldn\u2019t catch everything. As Rod Thorn, then the league\u2019s VP of operations, said at the time : \u201dthe game has become faster and quicker and is being played by bigger people, and it\u2019s our opinion that an extra pair of eyes would aid in covering the entire court more.\u201d But the last-second injury to referee Mark Lindsay during pregame warmups Thursday, which necessitated Brothers and Petraitis working the game alone, exposed the problem of not having an on-site fourth ref for regular season games, a practice the NBA uses for every postseason game. No, refs almost never get hurt during warmups, and two-man crews because of injuries are very rare. (And, in some cases, in some cities \u2014 like Philadelphia, for example, where a lot of referees live \u2014 the league can get a replacement ref who\u2019s off that night to a game in time if something odd like Lindsay\u2019s back spasms occurs.) But it happened Thursday. And that loss for the Rockets could ultimately mean the difference between hosting a Game 7 of the Western Conference finals in Houston against the Golden State Warriors, or having to go to Oakland for that Game 7. The NBA is already committed to hiring more refs \u2014 it will increase its pool from the current 64 to 70 by next season and by 25 percent over the next three years, with the additional refs sitting courtside as \u201cgame administrators\u201d to help the flow between the on-court refs and the league\u2019s Replay Center. That timetable should be sped up in time to have four refs on site for every regular season game starting next season. 2) Our friend Stu Jackson has a good idea that would alleviate the non-reviewable loophole for plays like Friday\u2019s obvious out of bounds deal with Giannis Antetokounmpo\u2019s last-second game-winning dunk against Oklahoma City \u2014 give a coach one challenge in the last two minutes of regulation. That would push back slightly against the league\u2019s desire to increase the pace of play, but it\u2019s a necessary brake for obvious missed plays like \u201cThe Greek Freak\u2019s\u201d dunk. 3) Have one of these in my closet somewhere . https:\/\/twitter.com\/NBATV\/status\/947589502742261762\/photo\/1 4) Please leave him behind in 2017. * * * MORE MORNING TIP: Movie-like storylines marked 2017 | DA\u2019s Top 15 Rankings | Rockets not fretting mini-slump | Q&A: Kris Dunn * * * Longtime NBA reporter, columnist and Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Famer David Aldridge is an analyst for TNT. The views on this page do not necessarily reflect the views of the NBA, its clubs or Turner Broadcasting."},{"id":42515,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-houston-rockets-not-fretting-losing-streak-james-harden-injury","date":"2018-01-01","title":"Houston Rockets keep their mini-slump in proper perspective","content":" The vagaries of an NBA season make almost every team look like Sasquatch one week and a Who in Whoville the next. The Houston Rockets looked invincible in November, winning 12 of 13, and snapped off 14 straight over the end of November and the beginning of December. They boatraced opponents, averaging 119.6 points per game and allowing just 103.4 , and shot almost 40 percent on 3-pointers. James Harden, Chris Paul, and Eric Gordon took turns from deep, with the usual support in kind from Trevor Ariza, Clint Capela and Ryan Anderson. The air was, rightly, full of talk that this was the team that could legitimately beat Golden State in a seven-game series. Then came December, and injuries to Paul, Capela and Luc Mbah a Moute, and the wheels came off. Paul, who\u2019d already missed 14 games earlier in the season with a bruised left knee, missed two games with a left adductor strain , but came back Friday. Capela returned on Sunday against the Lakers. But in the final minutes of regulation in the Rockets\u2019 double overtime win Sunday, which ended a five-game losing streak, Harden pulled up after a drive, and came up limping. He went straight to the locker room and didn\u2019t return, and was diagnosed with a strained hamstring . As of this morning, it\u2019s not known how long he\u2019ll be out. When Harden returns and gets back up to speed, the Rockets will certainly soon resume destroying opponents under a barrage of 3-pointers and rim runs, deflections and snuffed shots at the rim that lead to runouts, and fourth quarters for Harden and Paul with ice on their knees. But the temporary rough patch serves to illustrate how tenuous chemistry and momentum is to sustain over the six months of an NBA season, even for elite teams \u2014 and how opponents could potentially go after the Rockets in the playoffs. \u201cWe know what we have to do,\u201d an unconcerned Paul said after the loss to the Washington Wizards on Friday . \u201cWe have to get it right. We\u2019re not tripping, because we know how we play. I\u2019m a big believer in building and winning. I said that a long time ago. You don\u2019t need to learn stuff and lose. Learn stuff and win, and we done lost a few. All in all, we came out healthy. For us, that\u2019s part of the process. We\u2019re cool.\u201d For more than a week, though, everything went wrong \u2014 inexplicable back-to-back home losses to the Los Angeles Lakers and the LA Clippers before Christmas. There was a Christmas Day loss in Oklahoma City late , and an impossible collapse in Boston , with Houston blowing a 26-point first-half lead and then getting some bad calls in the last five minutes of the game. But it should have never gotten to that point in the first place. And the losing streak reached five Friday, the team\u2019s longest in almost five years, with a tired Rockets team not getting to D.C. until 3 a.m. They then got run out of Capital One Arena in the second half. \u201cIt\u2019s still there, but we\u2019ve just got to focus on what we really need to do,\u201d Gordon said. \u201cGolden State, they\u2019ve won championships. They know who they are. With us, we just need to continue to play the style of basketball we were early on \u2014 we were playing fast, playing, trusting each other on defense. Once we do that for a consistent year, then we can focus on Golden State. I just think we\u2019ve got to take it one step at a time. We\u2019ve still got a lot of new guys. Yeah, we were hot for a second, and we can get on another hot streak again. We\u2019re not really worried. But we\u2019ve got to do the little things.\u201d There\u2019s a reason Harden was all in for getting Paul. His absence put that weight vest of expectations right back on Harden, a burden he carried heroically all last season, but which overwhelmed him in the playoffs. In the postseason, Harden shot 41.3 percent overall and 27.8 percent on 3-pointers , tapping out with a horrific 2 of 11 performance in a 39-point loss to the San Antonio Spurs in the Western Conference semifinals. The Rockets couldn\u2019t afford for Harden to run out of gas again. But it\u2019s imperative that Paul be upright and in uniform in May and June. \u201cWe ask so much of James, and that\u2019s why we went out and got Chris,\u201d Rockets coach Mike D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cBecause James was making every determining play, and he gets tired. Anybody would. So there are moments where he\u2019s completely overloaded, and he has a turnover. And now, we can take all those plays away from him \u2014 when he\u2019s making, instead of 50 decisions, let\u2019s say 40, or 30. It\u2019s 30 without being tired decisions. That\u2019s huge.\u201d The impact of Paul\u2019s absence was obvious \u2014 an all-world ballhandler who can create, score and pass at an elite level while offering terrific on-ball and help defense. And for Houston, Paul\u2019s impact on Harden alone is worth whatever deal the Rockets work out with him, whether now (Paul is now eligible for a contract extension) or next summer, when he hits unrestricted free agency. No one around the league expects anything other than him re-signing with Houston. But the absence of Mbah a Moute, out since dislocating his right shoulder Dec. 13, has impacted Houston more than you\u2019d think. His defensive bona fides should go without saying at this point and having him on the floor with P.J. Tucker at the end of games gives the Rockets multiple switching options defensively. Offensively, Mbah a Moute has struggled so far on corner 3-pointers \u2014 just 7 of 30 so far, per NBA.com\/Stats \u2014 he\u2019s been extremely good getting the ball to the front of the rim on drives and cuts , as most are who play off of Harden and Paul.  Capela\u2019s absence may be the biggest of all, both short and long term. Houston\u2019s demeanor changes completely when the 23-year-old isn\u2019t on the floor. He missed the two games before Sunday with a right orbital fracture \u2026 after missing two of three games before that with a bruised heel. The Rockets want to keep his backup, Nene, healthy for the playoffs and he\u2019s on a strict non- back-to-back schedule during the regular season. But when he\u2019s pressed into service when Capela\u2019s out, that has a ripple effect. \u201cThe thing that Clint does is, we spread the floor open,\u201d Gordon said. \u201cWith him, he\u2019s catching lobs. And when he\u2019s not there, we don\u2019t throw lobs, hardly, to anybody to put pressure on the defense. And, he\u2019s a rim protector. We don\u2019t have a true, true rim protector when he\u2019s not there. He definitely plays a major role, for sure. He plays a major role in what we do.\u201d D\u2019Antoni has tried to make things as easy as possible, eliminating shootarounds. Houston arrives at its road destination early enough the day before to practice and go over opponents then, rather than the morning of the game. \u201cWe think rest is more important and we cover the opposing team the day before in practice,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said, adding that he can call an audible when necessary. \u201cWe feel the determining factor for us is having the right energy.\u201d Even though General Manager Daryl Morey has made no secret of the fact that he\u2019s got nothing but the Warriors on his mind, Paul seems to want his group to emulate the San Antonio Spurs rather than Golden State. \u201cIt\u2019s no secret they\u2019re the defending champions,\u201d he said of the Warriors. \u201cThey\u2019ve won the West, what, three years in a row? So until somebody beats them, they\u2019re the reigning champs. You can do that if you want to, but it\u2019s a league that changes. It changes. We were No. 1 in the West a couple of days ago. When you\u2019ve been around long enough, you realize it\u2019s all about how you\u2019re playing. Where\u2019s San Antonio right now? Told they were just behind Houston after the Rockets\u2019 losing streak, Paul said, \u201cthey ain\u2019t tripping. They just want to get their guys healthy.\u201d If Paul\u2019s not on the floor, teams get much more aggressive against Houston. The Celtics picked up Harden full court for long stretches Thursday, looking to wear him down, and did the same whenever Gordon brought up the ball. It led to a lot more one-pass-and-shoot shots for the Rockets rather than the ball whipping around like it normally does. And Harden and Gordon were just 5 of 27 combined from the floor in the second half and overtime. Now, Houston must wait for Harden to heal before it can get back on track. With back to back games in Orlando Wednesday and against the Warriors at Toyota Center Thursday, one would guess \u201cThe Beard\u201d would take off Wednesday to have a chance to play against the champs the next night. The Rockets beat Golden State on opening night with their full squad, but Paul then went out with the bruised knee. \u201cWe know that we\u2019re going to be up there,\u201d Gordon said. \u201cWe just need to concentrate on what we need to do. We were hot, we was doing all the little things, helping each other. Now, we\u2019ve hit a skid where offensively, we\u2019re not \u2026 Golden State, I look at them, they\u2019re getting almost 30 assists a night, and we\u2019re not doing that, and we play just as fast as they do. That\u2019s the point we\u2019ve got to get to, moving the ball and helping each other on defense. That\u2019s what we\u2019ve got to realize: once that ball moves, everybody scores, in big numbers. You can\u2019t score big numbers if that assist number ain\u2019t going up.
